<exec when="init">
def setupMaxDiffFile(fname, fileDelimiter="\t"):
    try:
        f = open("%s/%s" % (gv.survey.path, fname))
        mdObj = [ line.strip("\r\n").split(fileDelimiter) for line in f.readlines() ]
        d = dict( ("v%s_t%s" % (row[0], row[1]), row[2:]) for row in mdObj )
    except IOError:
        d = {}
    return d

def setupMaxDiffItemsI(d, vt, question):
    item_index = dict( (r.o.label.strip("item"), r.index) for r in question.rows )

    items = d[vt]

    for r in question.rows:
        if r.o.label.strip("item") not in items:
            r.disabled = True

    question.rows.order = [ item_index[i] for i in items ]

    print "*****STAFF ONLY*****"
    print "Version_Task: %s" % vt
    for i in range(len(items)):
        print "Item %s: %s" % (i+1,items[i])
        p.maxdiff1.append(items[i])
</exec>

def Prompt1(Qid):
 for i in Qid.rows:
	if Qid[i].displayed and not(Qid[i].any) and p.pri1==0:
		error(res.PROMPTERROR1)
		p.pri1=1
</exec>

<exec when="init">

		error(res.PROMPTERROR1)
		p.pri1=1
</exec>

<exec when="init">
def Prompt4(Qid):
	initarr=0
	for i in Qid.rows:
		if i.displayed and len(i.val) gt 0:
			initarr=1
			break
	if initarr==0 and p.pri1==0:
		error(res.PROMPTERROR)
		p.pri1=1
</exec>

def Punch4(Qid):
	initarr=0
	for i in Qid.rows:
		if i.displayed and not(i.val == "None" or i.empty):
			initarr=1
			break
	if initarr==0:
		Qid.r99.val=1
	p.pri1=0
</exec>

<exec when="init">
def zipCodeFile(fname, zipHeader):
  try:
      zipCodesData = File( "%s/%s" % (gv.survey.path, fname), zipHeader)
  except IOError:
      zipCodesData = ""
  return zipCodesData
</exec>

<html label="Maxdiff_Intro" where="survey"><p>
    In this section, you’ll see a series of short statements expressing different points of view. Each statement reflects a way of thinking about issues people often care deeply about including health, healthcare, community and politics.


  </p><br />

    For each set, please choose:
  </p>

  <ul>
    <li />The statement that sounds MOST like your own point of view, and
    <li />The statement that sounds LEAST like your own point of view.
  </ul>

  <p>
    <br /><em>Some statements may appear again later. That’s intentional — it helps us understand how people
    think across different kinds of ideas.</em>
  </p>

  <p>
    There are no right or wrong answers. Simply go with your first reaction each time.
  </p></html>

<text 
  label="XPOLICY"
  ss:listDisplay="0"
  where="execute,survey,report">
  <title>HIDDEN: POLICY</title>
  <exec>
POLICY_U = [5.4272, 4.7623, 6.0595]
POLICY_S = [1.24298, 1.74011, 0.99203]
POLICY_F = [float(x+1) for x in POLICY.values]
POLICY_AVG = [] 
   
for i in range(3):
 XPOLICY.rows[i].val = (POLICY_F[i] - POLICY_U[i])/POLICY_S[i]
 POLICY_AVG.append((POLICY_F[i] - POLICY_U[i])/POLICY_S[i])
 
XDEM_SEG.r11.c1.val = POLICY_F
XDEM_SEG.r11.c2.val = POLICY_U
XDEM_SEG.r11.c3.val = POLICY_S
XDEM_SEG.r11.c4.val = sum(POLICY_AVG) / len(POLICY_AVG)
  </exec>

  <row label="r1">The government should create a public insurance option to compete with private plans</row>
  <row label="r2">Health insurance should be provided through a single national health insurance system run by the government.</row>
  <row label="r3">Large employers should be required to provide health insurance to their workers.</row>
</text>

<block label="DEMBlock" cond="TYPING_MODULE.r2" builder:title="DEM Block">
  <note>MaxDiff Indices Template --Start1--</note>
  <exec when="init">
QMD1_md = setupMaxDiffFile("DemDesign.dat")
  </exec>

  <suspend/>

  <quota label="DemQuota" overquota="noqual" sheet="Dem Quota"/>

  <suspend/>

  <number 
   label="QMD1_Version"
   size="3"
   verify="range(1,100)"
   where="execute,survey,report">
    <title>QMD1 - MaxDiff Version<br /><br /><em>Pick your version for testing... will be automated when live...</em></title>
    <exec>
print p.markers
for x in p.markers:

def algorithmCalculation(resp_answers, segment_coeff):
    return sum((a - c)**2 for a, c in zip(resp_answers, segment_coeff))

def algorithmRaw(answers, constant_matrix):
    num_segments = len(constant_matrix[0])
    outputs = []
    for c in range(num_segments):

        segment_col = [row[c] for row in constant_matrix]
        output = algorithmCalculation(answers, segment_col)
        outputs.append(output)
    return outputs

p.resp_answers = [float(x) for x in XDEM_SEG.c4.values]

segment_matrix = [
    [-0.6195561, -0.1891442, -0.2056958, 0.2758133, 1.1020488, -0.4391141],
    [-0.1032678, -0.6410046, -0.5600926, 0.2196113, 0.5993271, 0.3670266],

    [0.429, -0.156, -0.023, -0.337, -0.2, 0],
    [0.049, 3.035, 1.486, 2.616, 0.522, 0]

    results.append(s)

  XQSEG_3.rows[i].val = results[i]

def algorithmCalculation(resp_answers, segment_coeff):
    return sum((a - c)**2 for a, c in zip(resp_answers, segment_coeff))

def algorithmRaw(answers, constant_matrix):
    num_segments = len(constant_matrix[0])
    outputs = []
    for c in range(num_segments):

        segment_col = [row[c] for row in constant_matrix]
        output = algorithmCalculation(answers, segment_col)
        outputs.append(output)
    return outputs

p.resp_answers1 = [float(x) for x in XGOP_SEG.c4.values]

    results2.append(s)

  <title>Model Agreement Status</title>
  <exec>

if TYPING_MODULE.r1:
    cent1 = XGOP_SEG_FINAL_1.val if XGOP_SEG_FINAL_1.any else None
    cent2 = XGOP_SEG_FINAL_2.val if XGOP_SEG_FINAL_2.any else None
    logit1 = XGOP1_SEG_FINAL_1.val if XGOP1_SEG_FINAL_1.any else None
    logit2 = XGOP1_SEG_FINAL_2.val if XGOP1_SEG_FINAL_2.any else None

elif TYPING_MODULE.r2:
    cent1 = XDEM_SEG_FINAL_1.val if XDEM_SEG_FINAL_1.any else None
    cent2 = XDEM_SEG_FINAL_2.val if XDEM_SEG_FINAL_2.any else None
    logit1 = XDEM1_SEG_FINAL_1.val if XDEM1_SEG_FINAL_1.any else None
    logit2 = XDEM1_SEG_FINAL_2.val if XDEM1_SEG_FINAL_2.any else None
else:
    cent1 = cent2 = logit1 = logit2 = None

if cent1 and logit1:
    if cent1 == logit1 and cent2 == logit2:
        # Full agreement - both #1 and #2 match
        XMODEL_AGREEMENT.val = XMODEL_AGREEMENT.r1.index
    elif cent1 == logit1 or cent2 == logit2:
        # Partial agreement - only one matches
        XMODEL_AGREEMENT.val = XMODEL_AGREEMENT.r2.index
    else:
        # No agreement
        XMODEL_AGREEMENT.val = XMODEL_AGREEMENT.r3.index
  </exec>

  <row label="r1">Full Agreement (Both #1 and #2 match)</row>
  <row label="r2">Partial Agreement (One matches)</row>
  <row label="r3">No Agreement</row>

  <title>Confidence Level Classification</title>
  <exec>
full_agreement = False
if XMODEL_AGREEMENT.any:
    full_agreement = (XMODEL_AGREEMENT.r1.val == 1)

dist1 = 99.0
if XCENTROID_DIST1.val is not None:
    dist1 = float(XCENTROID_DIST1.val)

rel_diff = 0.0
if XREL_DIFF.val is not None:
    rel_diff = float(XREL_DIFF.val)

logit_prob = 0.0
if XLOGIT_PROB1.val is not None:
    logit_prob = float(XLOGIT_PROB1.val)

low_conf = False
if XMODEL_AGREEMENT.any:
    if XMODEL_AGREEMENT.r3.val == 1:
        low_conf = True

if dist1 &gt;= 0.5:
    low_conf = True
    
if not (rel_diff &gt; 0.2):
    low_conf = True
    
if not (logit_prob &gt; 50):
    low_conf = True

if full_agreement and not (dist1 &gt;= 0.5) and rel_diff &gt; 0.5 and logit_prob &gt; 70:
    XCONF_LEVEL.val = XCONF_LEVEL.r1.index
elif low_conf:
    XCONF_LEVEL.val = XCONF_LEVEL.r3.index
else:
    XCONF_LEVEL.val = XCONF_LEVEL.r2.index
  </exec>

  <row label="r1">High Confidence</row>
  <row label="r2">Moderate Confidence</row>
  <row label="r3">Low Confidence</row>
</radio>

<suspend/>

<exec sst="0">
seg = XSEG_ASSIGNED.selected.index + 1
quota_cells = gv.survey.root.quota.getQuotaCells()

current1, limit1, overquota1 = quota_cells["/Wave One Equal Allocation QUOTA/XSEG_ASSIGN{}/MA_SEC".format(seg)]
current2, limit2, overquota2 = quota_cells["/Wave One Equal Allocation QUOTA/XSEG_ASSIGN{}/ESI_SEC".format(seg)]
current3, limit3, overquota3 = quota_cells["/Wave One Equal Allocation QUOTA/XSEG_ASSIGN{}/GLP_SEC".format(seg)]
current4, limit4, overquota4 = quota_cells["/Wave One Equal Allocation QUOTA/XSEG_ASSIGN{}/PREG_SEC".format(seg)]
current5, limit5, overquota5 = quota_cells["/Wave One Equal Allocation QUOTA/XSEG_ASSIGN{}/AL_SEC".format(seg)]
current6, limit6, overquota6 = quota_cells["/Wave One Equal Allocation QUOTA/XSEG_ASSIGN{}/VAX_SEC".format(seg)]
current7, limit7, overquota7 = quota_cells["/Wave One Equal Allocation QUOTA/XSEG_ASSIGN{}/VICP_SEC".format(seg)]

remain_MA = limit1 - current1
remain_ESI = limit2 - current2
remain_GLP = limit3 - current3
remain_PREG = limit4 - current4
remain_AL = limit5 - current5
remain_VAX = limit6 - current6
remain_VICP = limit7 - current7


# Quota open? (1 = open, 0 = closed)
q_MA   = 1 if (limit1 - current1) &gt; 0 else 0
q_ESI  = 1 if (limit2 - current2) &gt; 0 else 0
q_GLP  = 1 if (limit3 - current3) &gt; 0 else 0
q_PREG = 1 if (limit4 - current4) &gt; 0 else 0
q_AL   = 1 if (limit5 - current5) &gt; 0 else 0
q_VAX  = 1 if (limit6 - current6) &gt; 0 else 0
q_VICP = 1 if (limit7 - current7) &gt; 0 else 0

# =====================
# STUDY WEIGHTS (from screener responses)
# =====================

# MA: w=0 if uninsured, w=2 if MA enrolled, else w=1
if QINS1.r2:
    w_MA = 0
elif QINS3.r2:
    w_MA = 2
else:
    w_MA = 1

# ESI: w=0 if uninsured, w=2 if employer insurance, else w=1
if QINS1.r2:
    w_ESI = 0
elif QINS2.r1 or QINS2.r2 or QINS2.r3:
    w_ESI = 2
else:
    w_ESI = 1

# GLP1: w=2 for everyone
w_GLP = 2

# PREG: w=4 if currently pregnant, w=3 if planning/new parent, else w=0
if QPR1.r1:
    w_PREG =4
elif QPR1.r2 or QPR1.r3:
    w_PREG = 3
else:
    w_PREG = 0

# AL, VAX, VICP: w=1 for everyone
w_AL = 6
w_VAX = 1
w_VICP = 1

# =====================
# SEGMENT WEIGHTS (target/actual ratio)
# For now using static weights from spec; replace with dynamic calculation
# =====================

# =====================
# SEGMENT WEIGHTS (from spec)
# =====================


sw_ESI = 1 
sw_MA = 1
sw_GLP = 1 
sw_PREG = 1
sw_AL = 3 
sw_VAX = 2
sw_VICP = 2 


# =====================
# ELIGIBILITY (from Flag_prism - which studies not yet completed)
# =====================

elig_MA   = 1 if Flag_prism.r1 else 0
elig_ESI  = 1 if Flag_prism.r1 else 0
elig_GLP  = 1 if Flag_prism.r2 else 0
elig_PREG = 1 if Flag_prism.r4 else 0
elig_AL   = 1 
elig_VAX  = 1 
elig_VICP = 1 

# =====================
# FINAL SCORES = STUDY_WEIGHT x SEGMENT_WEIGHT x QUOTA_OPEN x ELIGIBILITY
# =====================

score_MA   = w_MA   * sw_MA   * q_MA   * elig_MA
score_ESI  = w_ESI  * sw_ESI  * q_ESI  * elig_ESI
score_GLP  = w_GLP  * sw_GLP  * q_GLP  * elig_GLP
score_PREG = w_PREG * sw_PREG * q_PREG * elig_PREG
score_AL   = w_AL   * sw_AL   * q_AL   * elig_AL
score_VAX  = w_VAX  * sw_VAX  * q_VAX  * elig_VAX
score_VICP = w_VICP * sw_VICP * q_VICP * elig_VICP

# Store for debugging/audit trail
p.score_MA   = score_MA
p.score_ESI  = score_ESI
p.score_GLP  = score_GLP
p.score_PREG = score_PREG
p.score_AL   = score_AL
p.score_VAX  = score_VAX
p.score_VICP = score_VICP

# =====================
# FIND WINNER (highest score, randomize ties)
# =====================

scores = [
    (score_ESI,  1, 'ESI'),
    (score_MA,   2, 'MA'),
    (score_GLP,  3, 'GLP'),
    (score_PREG, 4, 'PREG'),
    (score_AL,   5, 'AL'),
    (score_VAX,  6, 'VAX'),
    (score_VICP, 7, 'VICP'),
]

max_score = max(s[0] for s in scores)

p.flag_softterm = 0
p.XRANDOMPICK_val=0
if max_score == 0:
    # No valid path - soft terminate
    p.flag_softterm = 1
    p.winning_block = 'NONE'
else:
    # Get all tied for highest
    winners = [s for s in scores if s[0] == max_score]
    
    # Randomize among ties
    import random
    winner = random.choice(winners)


    XRANDOMPICK.val = winner[1]-1
    p.winning_score = winner[0]
    p.winning_block = winner[2]
    p.XRANDOMPICK_val = winner[1]


# Debug output

if p.XRANDOMPICK_val lt 1 or p.XRANDOMPICK_val gt 7:
	p.flag_softterm = 1
	p.winning_block = 'ERROR' # Audit trail 
	p.XRANDOMPICK_val = XRANDOMPICK.val
	

print "Segment:", seg
print "Quotas remaining - MA:{} ESI:{} GLP:{} PREG:{} AL:{} VAX:{} VICP:{}".format(remain_MA, remain_ESI, remain_GLP, remain_PREG, remain_AL, remain_VAX, remain_VICP)
print "Study weights - MA:{} ESI:{} GLP:{} PREG:{} AL:{} VAX:{} VICP:{}".format(w_MA, w_ESI, w_GLP, w_PREG, w_AL, w_VAX, w_VICP)
print "Segment weights - MA:{:.2f} ESI:{:.2f} GLP:{:.2f} PREG:{:.2f} AL:{:.2f} VAX:{:.2f} VICP:{:.2f}".format(sw_MA, sw_ESI, sw_GLP, sw_PREG, sw_AL, sw_VAX, sw_VICP)
print "Final scores - MA:{:.2f} ESI:{:.2f} GLP:{:.2f} PREG:{:.2f} AL:{:.2f} VAX:{:.2f} VICP:{:.2f}".format(score_MA, score_ESI, score_GLP, score_PREG, score_AL, score_VAX, score_VICP)
print "Winner:", p.winning_block
print "Flag_softterm", p.flag_softterm
</exec>

<radio 
  label="XRANDOMPICK"

        <html label="ESIMaxdiff_Intro" where="survey">You’ll see a series of short statements expressing different points of view. Each statement reflects a point of view about employer-sponsored insurance. For each set, please choose the one statement you find <strong>MOST</strong> compelling and the one statement you find <strong>LEAST</strong> compelling. <br /><br /><em>Some statements may appear again later. That’s intentional—it helps us understand how people think about ideas in various contexts. </em>There are no right or wrong answers. Simply go with your first reaction each time.</html>

        <loop label="QESI_md_loop" vars="task">
          <title>QESI - MaxDiff Loop</title>
          <block label="QESI_md_block" randomize="1">

        label="QESI_[loopvar: task]"
        adim="cols"

        ss:questionClassNames="QESI_maxdiff"
        unique="1">
              <title>Select the one statement that is <strong>MOST</strong> compelling to your own point of view  (on the left), and the statement that <strong>LEAST</strong> compelling you (on the right)</title>
              <exec>
setupMaxDiffItemsI( QESI_md, "v%d_t%d" % (QESI_Version.val, [loopvar: task]), QESI_[loopvar: task])
p.MDcount = str(QESI_md_loop_expanded.order.index([loopvar: task]-1)+1)
              </exec>

              <col label="best"><strong>MOST</strong> compelling</col>
              <col label="worst"><strong>LEAST</strong> compelling</col>
              <row label="item1">Employer-sponsored insurance shields families from rising medical costs—covering about 80–90 percent of all claims and preventing unexpected bills from becoming financial crises.</row>
              <row label="item2">Employer-sponsored insurance provides complete protection, covering medical, drug, maternity, and mental health care together in one plan so nothing important is left out.</row>
              <row label="item3">Workers stay protected through life changes, with COBRA and retiree options that help them maintain coverage and keep their doctors when jobs or family circumstances change.</row>
              <row label="item4">Employer-sponsored insurance connects employees and families to leading doctors, hospitals, and new treatments—the cornerstone of America’s private health care system that drives innovation and access to advanced care.</row>
              <row label="item5">Employer-sponsored insurance helps keep the health system competitive—by letting businesses and employees select the plans and providers that best fit their needs.</row>
              <row label="item6">Digital tools put employees in control of their coverage—to see costs in advance, track approvals, follow treatment plans and make confident, informed decisions.</row>
              <row label="item7">Employer-sponsored insurance expands convenience through telehealth, 24-hour nurse lines, and virtual mental health services that meet people where they are.</row>
              <row label="item8">Employers tailor benefits to their own workforce, offering coverage options like obesity treatment, fertility, and mental health programs that reflect employee priorities and the company’s values.</row>
              <row label="item9">Employer-sponsored insurance rewards work through a true partnership between employers and employees—turning shared payroll contributions and tax-free benefits into dependable coverage that employees earned.</row>
              <row label="item10">Employer-sponsored insurance has been a basic promise between employers and employees—hard work earns security and peace of mind. Taxing or weakening those benefits breaks that promise and erodes workplace trust between employers and employees.</row>
              <row label="item11">Employer-sponsored insurance channels tax-free private dollars to meet Americans’ health care needs keeping coverage affordable for families while reducing the burden on taxpayer-funded programs.</row>
              <row label="item12">Employers use their collective purchasing power to drive competition among hospitals, doctors, and drug companies—helping improve the quality of care while controlling costs.</row>
              <row label="item13">Employer-sponsored insurance drives medical progress—partnering with top health systems and innovators to expand access to advanced therapies while keeping care affordable for working families.</row>
              <row label="item14">Employers hold plans accountable for quality and spending, tracking data and outcomes to ensure every premium dollar strengthens employee health, not administrative overhead.</row>
              <row label="item15">Employers invest directly in workers’ health through wellness programs, preventive care incentives, and disease management support that keep people healthy and productive.</row>

              <title>Select the one statement that is <strong>MOST</strong> compelling to your own point of view  (on the left), and the statement that <strong>LEAST</strong> compelling you (on the right)</title>
              <exec>

p.MDcount = str(QMA_md_loop_expanded.order.index([loopvar: task]-1)+1)
              </exec>

              <col label="best"><strong>MOST</strong> compelling</col>
              <col label="worst"><strong>LEAST</strong> compelling</col>
              <row label="item1">Medicare Advantage offers one simple plan with stable premiums and coverage seniors can rely on—unlike traditional Medicare’s patchwork of providers and fees.</row>
              <row label="item2">Medicare Advantage shields retirees from crushing medical debt by capping annual out-of-pocket costs—financial protection traditional Medicare doesn’t provide.</row>
              <row label="item3">Medicare Advantage earns the trust of its members through strict federal audits and quality-based payments that hold every plan accountable for results.</row>
              <row label="item4">Medicare Advantage brings doctors, prescriptions, and benefits together in one coordinated plan so care is seamless, not fragmented like traditional Medicare.</row>
              <row label="item5">Medicare Advantage empowers seniors to choose doctors and benefits that fit their lives instead of a one-size-fits-all government design.</row>
              <row label="item6">Medicare Advantage covers the whole person—with dental, vision, hearing, and fitness benefits that traditional Medicare leaves out.</row>
              <row label="item7">Medicare Advantage modernizes care through telehealth and digital tools that keep members connected anywhere, unlike Medicare’s paper-driven system.</row>
              <row label="item8">Medicare Advantage rewards a lifetime of work by turning savings into lower premiums and better benefits for the people who earned them.</row>
              <row label="item9">Medicare Advantage stands beside patients with complex or chronic conditions, coordinating specialists and care managers that traditional Medicare doesn’t provide.</row>
              <row label="item10">Seniors chose Medicare Advantage on a promise of dependable care. Cutting benefits breaks that promise and betrays the trust people placed in the program.</row>
              <row label="item11">Medicare Advantage reinvests plan savings directly into seniors’ benefits—proof that efficiency can serve people, not profit.</row>
              <row label="item12">Medicare Advantage delivers better outcomes at lower cost by paying for coordinated, effective care instead of rewarding volume like traditional Medicare.</row>
              <row label="item13">Medicare Advantage protects seniors’ independence and saves money through preventive care and early detection that prevent costly illness and hospitalization.</row>
              <row label="item14">Medicare Advantage ensures every dollar goes to patient care by tying payments to performance and quality outcomes.</row>
              <row label="item15">Medicare Advantage strengthens—not replaces—Medicare by combining public oversight with private innovation to meet today’s medical realities.</row>

        <title>CRITIC1 - MaxDiff Loop</title>
        <block label="CRITIC1_md_block" randomize="1">
          <radio 
       label="CRITIC1_[loopvar: task]"
       adim="cols"
       grouping="cols"
       shuffle="rows"
       ss:questionClassNames="CRITIC1_maxdiff"
       unique="1">
            <title><span>Select one statement you find MOST compelling (button on the left) and the one statement you find LEAST compelling (button on the right).</span></title>
            <exec>
setupMaxDiffItemsI( CRITIC1_md, "v%d_t%d" % (CRITIC1_Version.val, [loopvar: task]), CRITIC1_[loopvar: task])
p.MDcount = str(CRITIC1_md_loop_expanded.order.index([loopvar: task]-1)+1)
            </exec>

            <col label="best"><strong>MOST compelling</strong></col>
            <col label="worst"><strong>LEAST compelling</strong></col>
            <row label="item1">Compounded GLP-1s are risky because they aren’t regulated like the brand name drugs they claim to copy. They may be contaminated, have the wrong dose of medicine, or not have the right medicine at all.</row>
            <row label="item2">Compounded GLP-1s aren’t tested in large placebo-controlled studies like brand name drugs — so patients don’t know if they are safe or effective.</row>
            <row label="item3">Compounded GLP-1s are being sold online, in beauty salons, and spas. Patients have no way of knowing what they are getting in their medicine — or if it is even medicine at all.</row>
            <row label="item4">It doesn’t make sense to have two different sets of rules for medicines — one for brand name medicines that are tested and reviewed by the FDA and one for compounded medicines that don’t have to prove anything.</row>
            <row label="item5">Because compounders don’t do clinical trials, they are essentially experimenting on all the patients who take their medicine.</row>
            <row label="item6">Unsafe compounding has led to deaths and illness in the past. We shouldn’t wait for that tragedy to repeat before taking action to stop illegal compounding.</row>
            <row label="item7">Since these compounded drugs aren’t tested, you can’t trust that each dose is the same. While one may not be harmful, the next one may be.</row>
            <row label="item8">Mass compounders are lying when they claim to “personalize” drugs. They’re giving the same version to everyone.</row>
            <row label="item9">Compounders are claiming to “personalize” medicines to get around the law against mass-producing compounded medicines — not for medical reasons.</row>
            <row label="item10">Buying a compounded medicine is like buying a fake handbag off the street — except you are injecting the medicine in your body without knowing what’s in it.</row>
            <row label="item11">[pipe: XCRITIC1_1]</row>
            <row label="item12">[pipe: XCRITIC1_2]</row>
            <row label="item13">Compounders are skirting federal compounding rules to gain an unfair advantage — operating outside the guardrails that legitimate pharmacies and manufacturers follow.</row>
            <row label="item14">Medicines that are not tested and FDA-approved are riskier than those that are.</row>
            <row label="item15">Online pharmacies and others who push compounded GLP-1s often mislead consumers into believing their medicines are FDA-approved when they are not.</row>
            <row label="item16">Some compounders leave out or hide important information about what patients are getting and the risks — keeping people from having accurate information to make informed decisions.</row>
            <row label="item17">Many online compounders use short, low-quality telehealth visits that act as “rubber stamps,” blurring the line between real care and just filling an order.</row>
            <row label="item18">Compounders are ripping off Americans by selling fake GLP-1s and pretending they are safe and effective, like brand name medicines.</row>
            <row label="item19">Employers and insurers should do a better job covering GLP-1s so that people aren’t pushed to take unproven knock-off drugs.</row>
            <row label="item20">A two-tier system is emerging where wealthier patients get tested, FDA-approved medicines while lower-income and marginalized communities are left with unsafe compounded knockoffs.</row>

     label="QBIOPH_Version"
     size="3"
     verify="range(1,100)"
     where="execute,survey,report">
        <title>QBIOPH - MaxDiff Version<br /><br /><em>Pick your version for testing... will be automated when live...</em></title>
        <exec>
print p.markers
for x in p.markers:
    if "/Biopharma Quota/BIOPH_" in x:
        QBIOPH_Version.val = int(x.split("_")[-1])
        break
        </exec>

p.startTime = timeSpent()

      <html label="QBIOPHMaxdiff_Intro" where="survey">You’ll see a series of short statements expressing different points of view. Each statement reflects a point of view about investments being made by the biopharmaceutical industry. For each set, please choose the one statement you find <strong>MOST</strong> compelling and the one statement you find <strong>LEAST</strong> compelling.
        <br /><br /><em>Some statements may appear again later. That’s intentional—it helps us understand how people think about ideas in various contexts. There are no right or wrong answers. Simply go with your first reaction each time.</em></html>

          <radio 
       label="QBIOPH_[loopvar: task]"
       adim="cols"
       grouping="cols"
       shuffle="rows"
       ss:listDisplay="0"
       ss:questionClassNames="QBIOPH_maxdiff"
       unique="1">
            <title>Select the one statement that is <strong>MOST</strong> compelling to your own point of view  (on the left), and the statement that <strong>LEAST</strong> compelling you (on the right)</title>
            <exec>
setupMaxDiffItemsI( QBIOPH_md, "v%d_t%d" % (QBIOPH_Version.val, [loopvar: task]), QBIOPH_[loopvar: task])
p.MDcount = str(QBIOPH_md_loop_expanded.order.index([loopvar: task]-1)+1)
            </exec>

    <block label="BLOCK_AL_POSTTESTS" builder:title="American Leadership (AL) Post-Test">
      <radio 
     label="AL_POST"
     fir="off"
     grouping="rows"
     randomize="0"
     shuffle="rows"
     uses="cardrating.1">
        <title><span style="color: black;">Now that you have read more on the topic, how important is it for...</span></title>
        <comment><span style="font-size: 10pt;">Please select a button for each card.</span></comment>

          <row label="r1">Countries with fully government-funded health care may recommend fewer childhood vaccines because the government decides which medicines deliver sufficient value for the health system as a whole.</row>
          <row label="r2">Countries with universal health care can recommend fewer childhood vaccines overall because they can better screen children to determine those at greater risk.</row>

          </exec>

          <row label="r1">Countries like Denmark are often cited for having fewer routine childhood vaccines, but many other countries have childhood vaccine schedules that are similar to, or just as comprehensive as, the U.S. vaccine schedule.</row>
          <row label="r2">The goal in the United States should not be to use fewer vaccines simply to match other countries, but rather  should be based on what puts American children and patients first.</row>

              <row label="item1">Vaccines save more for society than they cost us by preventing illness before it starts or making it less severe.</row>
              <row label="item2">The vaccines on the childhood immunization schedule have been studied for longer, in more people, and in more real-world settings than almost any other medical intervention. Conducting additional placebo-controlled trials of these vaccines  is a waste of valuable resources when we have decades of consistent, population-level safety and effectiveness data.</row>
              <row label="item3">School vaccine rules are needed to stop outbreaks that are becoming more frequent, including the Measles outbreak that is spreading across the country.  Measles outbreaks can cause needless suffering for young children, including hearing loss, brain damage and death.</row>
              <row label="item4">No federal law mandates childhood vaccinations. School-entry requirements are set at the state level, and allow for medical, religious and/or personal belief exemptions, giving parents wide latitude in decision-making.</row>
              <row label="item5">Vaccines are important not only for saving lives, but for helping to eradicate diseases like polio, measles and smallpox that caused immense suffering and lifelong disability that kids and parents should no longer have to fear.</row>
              <row label="item6">Childhood vaccines prevented over a million deaths in the past thirty years, Before vaccines, infectious diseases that are now prevented by vaccines were the primary cause of death, and the most dangerous time in life was being a child under five years old.</row>
              <row label="item7">The same guidelines and laws governing childhood vaccines have been in place for decades. Making dramatic changes to these guidelines won’t change the risk of vaccine side effects, but will certainly increase the risk of kids getting sick from diseases</row>
              <row label="item8">The public health response to COVID wasn't perfect, but if we undo childhood vaccination as a reaction we are putting our kids at serious risk without good evidence to back it up.</row>
              <row label="item9">Changing vaccine recommendations only makes things more confusing for parents and makes it harder to ensure that every child who needs a vaccine can get one. If the CDC’s guidance is just to talk to your doctor then the CDC doesn’t serve a useful purpose.</row>
              <row label="item10">Sowing doubt and making it harder for parents and doctors to vaccinate kids won’t make American kids healthier. Raising nutrition and fitness standards will do much more to ‘make America healthy again.’</row>

              <title>Select the one statement that is <strong>MOST</strong> compelling to your own point of view  (on the left), and the statement that <strong>LEAST</strong> compelling you (on the right)</title>
              <exec>



setupMaxDiffItemsI( QVICP_md, "v%d_t%d" % (QVICP_Version.val, [loopvar: task]), QVICP_[loopvar: task])
p.MDcount = str(QVICP_md_loop_expanded.order.index([loopvar: task]-1)+1)

              <col label="best"><strong>MOST</strong> compelling</col>
              <col label="worst"><strong>LEAST</strong> compelling</col>
              <row label="item1">For families dealing with serious injury, the Vaccine Injury Compensation Program is designed to deliver decisions and compensation more quickly than unpredictable jury trials.</row>
              <row label="item2">Unlike civil lawsuits, the program does not require an injured person to prove negligence or wrongdoing—only that a known injury occurred. The program includes a list of possible vaccine injuries.  If a person has one of those injuries they will be compensated.</row>
              <row label="item3">The program does not take away anyone’s right to go to court—it offers a faster, lower-stress option first, with lawsuits still available if needed.</row>
              <row label="item4">What’s at stake is balancing care for injured individuals with keeping vaccines affordable and available.The Vaccine Injury Compensation Program was designed to do both—compensate people fairly while avoiding legal uncertainty that raises costs and can take many years to resolve.</row>
              <row label="item5">Most childhood vaccines are low-cost products so the risk of unpredictable lawsuits led manufacturers to stop developing vaccines in the U.S. The compensation program was designed to keep vaccines available for children here in America.</row>
              <row label="item6">Weakening the Vaccine Injury Compensation Program would enrich a small number of personal injury lawyers instead of helping families in need. The no-fault system exists because it compensates injuries more reliably than lawsuits designed to chase large verdicts.</row>
              <row label="item7">A no-fault compensation system like the Vaccine Injury Compensation Program protects vaccine decisions from becoming political battles played out in courtrooms instead of guided by evidence and standards.</row>
              <row label="item8">Without the program, only families who can afford long legal battles would have a realistic chance of compensation.</row>
              <row label="item9">The Vaccine Injury Compensation Program program exists because everyone acknowledges that rare but serious vaccine injuries can happen. Having a system in place to deal with those cases makes the vaccine system more fair, reliable and accountable.</row>
              <row label="item10">Informed consent works best when people know there is a clear, fair system like the Vaccine Injury Compensation Program  to help if a vaccine causes a rare injury.</row>

jQuery(document).ready(function () {

    var $q = jQuery("#question_QPREG_VAX_WHO");

    function updateCheckboxState() {
        var $checks = $q.find("input[type='checkbox']");
        var checkedCount = $checks.filter(":checked").length;

        if (checkedCount >= maxAllowed) {
            $checks.not(":checked").prop("disabled", true);
        } else {
            $checks.prop("disabled", false);
        }
    }

    // Run when user changes selection
    $q.on("change", "input[type='checkbox']", updateCheckboxState);

    // Run when page loads / user comes back
    updateCheckboxState();
});

For each set, please choose the one statement you find <strong>MOST</strong> compelling and the one statement you find <strong>LEAST</strong> compelling.
<br /><br /><em>Some statements may appear again later. That’s intentional—it helps us understand how people think about ideas in various contexts.</em> There are no right or wrong answers. Simply go with your first reaction each time.</html>

    <title>CRITIC1 - MaxDiff Loop</title>
    <block label="QPREG_CRITIC1_md_block" randomize="1">
      <radio 
     label="QPREG_CRITIC1_[loopvar: task]"
     adim="cols"
     grouping="cols"
     shuffle="rows"
     ss:questionClassNames="CRITIC1_maxdiff"
     unique="1">
        <title>Select the one statement that is <strong>MOST</strong> compelling to your own point of view  (on the left), and the statement that <strong>LEAST</strong> compelling you (on the right)</title>
        <exec>
setupMaxDiffItemsI( CRITIC1_md, "v%d_t%d" % (QPREG_CRITIC1_Version.val, [loopvar: task]), QPREG_CRITIC1_[loopvar: task])
p.MDcount = str(QPREG_CRITIC1_md_loop_expanded.order.index([loopvar: task]-1)+1)
        </exec>

        <col label="best"><strong>MOST compelling</strong></col>
        <col label="worst"><strong>LEAST compelling</strong></col>
        <row label="item1">Babies are most vulnerable to serious infections in their first months of life. The vaccine schedule starts early so protection is in place when babies are most at risk—not after exposure.</row>
        <row label="item2">Spacing out vaccines may feel cautious, but it leaves babies unprotected for longer periods when infections can be most dangerous.</row>
        <row label="item3">Vaccines can cause mild side effects like soreness or a low fever, which are signs the immune system is responding. Serious reactions are extremely rare, and the diseases vaccines protect against pose far greater risks to children.</row>
        <row label="item4">Giving multiple vaccines at the same visit has not been shown to increase the risk of serious harm compared with spacing them out. The childhood vaccine schedule has been carefully studied to understand how vaccines work when they are given together, not just one at a time.</row>
        <row label="item5">[pipe: XQVAR1]</row>
        <row label="item6">[pipe: XQVAR2]</row>
        <row label="item7">Vaccine-preventable diseases are dangerous even when they aren’t fatal. Children who contract these diseases often endure severe illness, and survivors can be left with lifelong harm such as paralysis, hearing loss, or heart and lung damage.</row>
        <row label="item8">Before vaccines, early childhood was the most dangerous time of life because infectious diseases caused the highest risk of premature death. Childhood vaccines exist to prevent those same diseases from posing that level of risk today.</row>
        <row label="item9">When fewer pregnant women get recommended vaccines—even by a small amount—doctors see more preterm births, more severe illness in mothers, and more babies hospitalized.</row>
        <row label="item10">[pipe: XQVAR3]</row>
        <row label="item11">[pipe: XQVAR4]</row>
        <row label="item12">When a pregnant woman becomes seriously ill from an infection, the risk of preterm birth and infant hospitalization increases. Vaccination during pregnancy lowers the chance of severe illness in the mother, reducing these risks for the baby.</row>
        <row label="item13">[pipe: XQVAR5]</row>
        <row label="item14">[pipe: XQVAR6]</row>
        <row label="item15">Freedom also means being able to have my children go to preschool or the grocery store without being stalked by diseases that can be prevented.  Ensuring kids are vaccinated before going to school protects that freedom.</row>
        <row label="item16">Choosing not to vaccinate doesn’t eliminate risk—it shifts that risk onto other families, schools, and teachers. Most families vaccinate to keep schools safe, and it isn’t fair for others to rely on that protection while refusing to do the same.</row>
        <row label="item17">We don’t all have the luxury of “designer” health choices. When wealthy families assume their kids aren’t at risk and opt out of vaccines, outbreaks happen—and working families pay the price.</row>
        <row label="item18">Parents always have choices. Those who believe vaccines pose greater risk than disease often choose private or homeschooling. But other families deserve the peace of mind we’ve long taken for granted—that preventable diseases won’t spread in our communities.</row>
        <row label="item19">[pipe: XQVAR7]</row>

        $(left)
        ${"%s%s" % (elements.split("</td>")[1],"</td>")}
    </$(tag)>
\@endif
]]></style>
      </radio>
    </block>

  ESI_ROI_CAT.val = 6
    </exec>

  pers_mag = 1.5

    ESI_PERSUASION_CAT.ival == 4):

    </exec>

    <title>GLP1_INFLUENCE360</title>
    <exec>
vals = [
  GLP_QELECTED.r1.val, GLP_QELECTED.r2.val, GLP_QELECTED.r3.val, GLP_QELECTED.r4.val, GLP_QELECTED.r5.val,
  GLP_QELECTED.r6.val, GLP_QELECTED.r7.val, GLP_QELECTED.r8.val, GLP_QELECTED.r9.val, GLP_QELECTED.r10.val,
  GLP_QELECTED.r11.val, GLP_QELECTED.r12.val, GLP_QELECTED.r13.val, GLP_QELECTED.r14.val, GLP_QELECTED.r15.val,
  GLP_QELECTED.r16.val, GLP_QELECTED.r17.val, GLP_QELECTED.r18.val, GLP_QELECTED.r19.val
]

GLP1_INFLUENCE360.val = round(sum(vals) / 19.0, 4)
    </exec>

  </float>

  <float 
   label="ROI_GLP1"
   where="execute,survey,report">
    <title>ROI_GLP1</title>
    <exec>
conv = float(GLP1_PERSUADABILITY.ival) if GLP1_PERSUADABILITY.ival is not None else 0.5
sup  = float(GLP1_BASE_SUPPORT.ival)    if GLP1_BASE_SUPPORT.ival    is not None else 0.5
conv_norm = (conv + sup)/2.0
mob = float(GLP1_MOBILIZATION.ival)    if GLP1_MOBILIZATION.ival    is not None else 0.5
inf = float(GLP1_INFLUENCE360.ival)    if GLP1_INFLUENCE360.ival    is not None else 0.0
eng = (mob + inf)/2.0
ROI_GLP1.val = round((2.0 * conv_norm + eng) / 3.0,4)
    </exec>

  </float>

  <float 
   label="XFIELD_DATE_NUM"
   where="execute,survey,report">
    <title>DATE COMPLETED</title>
    <exec>
from datetime import datetime
XFIELD_DATE_NUM.val = float(datetime.utcnow().strftime('%Y%m%d'))
    </exec>

  </float>
</block>
</survey>
